Arguments for Absolute Negation: Divine Perfection and Initial Origination
Sanusi details the two arguments of the first type: the perfection argument and the initial origination argument, including objections and refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main arguments that prove it is impossible for God to act for a purpose, and how the Ash'aris respond to objections.

Core Idea
If God acted for a purpose, He would be imperfect; but everything originates from Him directly.

Sanusi presents the two key arguments from the first category (luzum al-nafy). These arguments aim to show that purpose is absolutely impossible in God's actions. He also includes the objections raised against them and the Ash'ari responses, which are important for understanding the depth of the debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument
Read the argument about divine perfection. Notice how it links purpose to deficiency.
2
Consider the objection and rebuttal
The objection says purpose could benefit another. Trace the rebuttal and the final refutation.
The final refutation denies the necessity that benefit must be better for God.
3
Read the second argument
This argument is about initial origination. Understand why a purpose would imply dependence.
4
Examine the second objection and its refutation
The objection allows interdependencies. Note how the Ash'ari respond by narrowing the concept of purpose.
The refutation points out that even pleasure may require intermediaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (وأما نفي الغرض) فمن أدلة القوم ما يفيد لزوم النفي كقولهم لو كان فاعلاً لغرض كان ناقصاً في ذاته مستكملاً بغيره. وقولهم قد ثبت استناد الكل إليه ابتداء من غير أن يكون البعض غرضاً وتبعاً للبعض، ومنها ما يفيد نفي اللزوم كقولهم لا بد من الانتهاء إلى ما يكون البعض لغرض قطعاً للسلسلة، وقولهم لا يعقل في مثل تخليد الكفار نفع لأحد، وهذا أقرب تعليل بعض الأفعال سيما شرعية الأحكام مما يشهد به النصوص، ويكاد يقع عليه الإجماع وبه يثبت القياس . ما ذهب إليه الأشاعرة أن أفعال الله تعالى ليست معللة بالأغراض، يفهم من : بعض أدلته عموم السلب ولزوم النفي بمعنى أنه يمتنع أن يكون شيء من أفعاله معللاً بالغرض، ومن بعضها سلب العموم ونفي اللزوم ، أي بمعنى أن ذلك ليس بلازم في كل فعل فمن الأول وجهان : أحدهما : لو كان الباري فاعلاً لغرض لكان ناقصاً في ذاته مستكملاً بتحصيل ذلك الغرض، لأنه لا بد في الغرض من أن يكون وجوده أصلح للفاعل من عدمه، وهو معنى الكمال، لا يقال لعل الغرض يعود إلى الغير فلا تتم الملازمة . لأنا نقول : وحصول ذلك الغرض للغير لابد أن يكون أصلح للفاعل من عدمه، وإلا لم يصلح غرضاً لفعله ضرورة، وحينئذ يعود الإلزام ، وردّ بمنع الضرورة، بل يكفي مجرد كونه أصلح للغير. وثانيهما : لو كان شيء من الممكنات غرضاً لفعل الباري لما كان حاصلاً بخلقه ابتداء بل بتبعية ذلك الفعل وتوسطه لأن ذلك معنى الغرض واللازم باطل لما ثبت استناد الكل إليه ابتداء من غير أن يكون البعض أولى بالغرضية والتبعية من البعض. لا يقال معنى استناد الكل إليه ابتداء أنه الموجد بالاستقلال لكل ممكن لا أن ممكناً. وذلك الممكن ممكناً آخر على ما يراه الفلاسفة. وهذا لا ينافي توقف تحصيل البعض على البعض كالحركة على الجسم ، والوصول إلى المنتهى على الحركة ونحو ذلك ما لا يحصى . لأنا نقول الذي يصلح أن يكون غرضاً لفعله ليس إلا إيصال اللذة إلى العبد، وهو مقدور له تعالى من غير شيء من الوسائط. وردّ بعد تسليم انحصار الغرض فيما ذكر بأن إيصال بعض اللذات قد لا يمكن إلا بخلق وسائط كالإحساس، ووجود ما يلتذ به ونحو ذلك . ومن الثاني وجهان: أحدهما أنه لا بد من انقطاع السلسلة إلى ما يكون غرضاً، ولا يكون لغرض، فلا يصح القول بلزوم الغرض وعمومه. وثانيهما أن مثل تخليد الكفار في النار لا يعقل فيه نفع لأحد، والحق أن تعليل بعض الأفعال لا سيما شرعية الأحكام بالحكم والمصالح ظاهر كايجاب الحدود، والكفارات، وتحريم المسكرات وما أشبه ذلك ، والنصوص أيضاً شاهدة بذلك كقوله تعالى وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون ومن أجل ذلك كتبنا على بني إسرائيل الآية فلما قضى زيد منها وطراً زوجناكها لكيلا يكون على المؤمنين حرج الآية ولهذا
He said: 'Regarding the negation of purpose, from the proofs of the people are those that entail the necessity of negation, such as their statement: if He were an agent for a purpose, He would be deficient in His essence, perfecting Himself through another. And their statement: it is established that everything originates from Him initially, without some being a purpose and subordinate to others. And among them are those that entail negation of necessity, such as their statement: there must be an end to a series with something that is a purpose, without itself being for a purpose, to cut the chain, and their statement: in something like immortalizing the disbelievers in the Fire, no benefit for anyone is conceivable. And this is closer to explaining some acts, especially the legal rulings, as witnessed by texts, and there is near consensus on it, and by it analogy is established. The Ash'ari school holds that the acts of God Most High are not caused by purposes. It is understood from some of their proofs: absolute negation and necessity of negation, meaning that it is impossible that any of His acts should be caused by a purpose; and from some of them: negation of universality and negation of necessity, meaning that this is not necessary in every act. So from the first [type] there are two arguments: First: if the Creator were an agent for a purpose, He would be deficient in His essence, perfecting Himself through the attainment of that purpose, because a purpose must involve its existence being better for the agent than its absence, which is the meaning of perfection. One cannot say: perhaps the purpose redounds to another, so the entailment does not hold. For we say: the attainment of that purpose for the other must be better for the agent than its absence, otherwise it would not be fit as a purpose for His act necessarily, and then the objection returns. It was refuted by denying the necessity; rather, merely its being better for the other suffices. Second: if something among possibles were a purpose for the Creator's act, it would not occur by His creation initially, but rather through the dependence on and intermediacy of that act, because that is the meaning of purpose. And the consequent is false because it is established that everything originates from Him initially, without some being more deserving of purposeness and subordination than others. One cannot say: the meaning of everything originating from Him initially is that He is the independent originator of every possible, not that one possible is not a possible for another, as the philosophers hold, and this does not contradict the dependence of the attainment of some on others, like motion on a body, and reaching the goal on motion, and the like of what is countless. For we say: that which can be a purpose for His act is only the conveyance of pleasure to the servant, and that is within His power Most High without any intermediaries. It was refuted after granting the restriction of purpose to what was mentioned, by saying that the conveyance of some pleasures may not be possible except through the creation of intermediaries like sensation and the existence of what is enjoyed and the like. And from the second [type] there are two arguments: First: there must be a termination of the chain to that which is a purpose but not for a purpose, so it is not correct to say that purpose is necessary and universal. Second: that something like immortalizing the disbelievers in the Fire cannot be conceived to benefit anyone. And the truth is that explaining some acts, especially legal rulings, by underlying causes and interests is apparent, like imposing fixed punishments, expiations, prohibition of intoxicants, and the like, and the texts also bear witness to that, such as His statement Most High: 'I did not create jinn and mankind except to worship Me' (Qur'an 51:56), and 'Because of that We prescribed for the Children of Israel' (Qur'an 5:32), and 'So when Zayd had completed his desire from her, We married her to you so that there be no restriction for the believers' (Qur'an 33:37). And for this...

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a painful trial, do you instinctively search for a hidden purpose or lesson? How does the Ash'ari teaching that God does not act for purposes challenge your need to find meaning in suffering? Can you trust His perfection without demanding an explanation? Commit today to stop asking 'why me' and instead say 'You are perfect, and I submit.'
?
Reflect on your last act of worship—was it performed purely for God's sake, or were you secretly seeking a reward, peace of mind, or a sense of accomplishment? The lesson teaches that God's actions are not motivated by purposes. Are yours? Examine your heart: will you perform your next prayer with the sole intention of obeying Him, without any expectation of benefit?
?
The belief that God acts for a purpose can make us feel that our lives must have a clear, discernible purpose. What if the truth is that God's freedom means He does not create us for a 'reason' we can grasp? Does that disturb you or liberate you? Let this lesson push you to surrender your need for a cosmic explanation and simply exist in worship of the Perfect One.

Arguments for Negation of Necessity and the Role of Wisdom
Sanusi presents the second type arguments and concludes that some acts are explained by wisdoms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two arguments that show purpose is not necessary in every divine act, and the Ash'ari affirmation that some acts, especially legal rulings, have underlying wisdoms.

Core Idea
Purpose is not necessary in all acts; some acts like punishing disbelievers have no apparent benefit.

Sanusi now turns to the second category of arguments, which aim to show that purpose is not necessary in every divine act. He gives two arguments: the termination of causal chains and the lack of benefit in eternal punishment. Then he affirms that some acts, especially legal rulings, are indeed based on wisdoms and interests, as supported by revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument
Understand the chain-termination argument: there must be an end to purposes.
2
Read the second argument
Consider the example of immortalizing disbelievers in Hell.
This shows that some acts have no conceivable benefit.
3
Read the concluding section
Sanusi affirms that explaining legal rulings by wisdoms is apparent and supported by texts.
Notice the Qur'anic verses cited.

Under the first type (luzum al-nafy), he gives two arguments:
1. If God acted for a purpose, He would be deficient in His essence, perfecting Himself through that purpose. The counterargument that the purpose might benefit another is rebutted because the benefit to another must still be better for God, otherwise it wouldn't be a purpose. However, this is refuted by denying that necessity – it suffices that it is better for the other.
2. If any possible thing were a purpose, it would depend on intermediacy, contradicting the fact that everything originates from God initially without mediation. The possible response that interdependence (like motion needing a body) is allowed is refuted by specifying that the only true purpose is conveying pleasure to the servant, which God can do without intermediaries. But this is further refuted by noting that some pleasures require intermediaries.

Under the second type (nafy al-luzum), he gives two arguments:
1. There must be an end to the chain of purposes – something that is a purpose but not itself for a purpose – so purpose cannot be universal or necessary.
2. Acts like immortalizing disbelievers in Hell have no conceivable benefit for anyone, so they cannot be for a purpose.

The passage concludes by affirming that explaining some acts, especially legal rulings, by underlying causes and interests is apparent and supported by texts, giving examples from the Qur'an.

Key Terms
نفي اللزوم
السلسلة
التعليل
الحكم
المصالح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari view completely rejects any purpose or wisdom in God's actions.
Correction: The Ash'aris only reject that God is motivated by purposes (which imply need), but they affirm that actions have wisdoms and interests, especially in legal rulings.

Checkpoint
What is the second argument of the second type?
A) Everything originates from God directly
B) There must be an end to the chain of purposes
C) Immortalizing disbelievers in Hell has no benefit
D) Legal rulings have underlying wisdoms

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari view denies that God is motivated by purposes but affirms that His actions have wisdoms, as seen in legal rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials that seem pointless, do you secretly doubt the wisdom behind them? How does Sanusi's argument that some acts have no apparent purpose challenge your expectations of God?
?
The passage mentions the eternal punishment of disbelievers – how does this reality confront the modern tendency to judge God's actions by human standards of fairness? Are you willing to accept that God's wisdom may be beyond your comprehension?
?
You often want to see immediate benefit in your acts of worship. How does the Ash'ari teaching free you from expecting worldly returns, and what does it demand of your faith?

Purpose is Not Necessary in Divine Acts
Refutes necessity of purpose and mediation argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the necessity of purpose in God's actions is rejected and how the argument from mediation fails.

Core Idea
God's acts do not require a purpose; it is enough that they benefit others.

This lesson tackles the initial objection that all divine actions must have a purpose. The author first denies this necessity and then refutes the idea that contingent things could serve as purposes requiring mediation. We'll see why direct divine action is sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source and its English translation carefully. Notice the structure of objection and response.
The passage is dense; take it slowly.
2
Identify the objection and first response
The objection says purpose is necessary. The author denies the necessity and offers a simpler alternative: 'it is sufficient that it is for the benefit of others.' Mark this contrast.
3
Examine the second argument about mediation
The second claim is that if a contingent thing were a purpose, it would require mediation. The author counters that everything depends directly on God. A counterargument from the philosophers is considered and refuted.
Focus on the idea that God can convey pleasure without means.
4
Reflect on the objection about means
The objector says some pleasures need means like sensation. The author concedes this but holds it does not prove purpose is necessary for all acts.
This sets up the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غرضاً لفعله ضرورة، وحينئذ يعود الإلزام، وردّ بمنع الضرورة، بل يكفي مجرد كونه من أصلح للغير. وثانيهما: لو كان شيء من الممكنات غرضاً لفعل الباري لما كان حاصلاً بخلقه ابتداء بل بتبعية ذلك الفعل وتوسطه لأن ذلك (۱) معنى الغرض واللازم باطل لما ثبت استناد الكل إليه ابتداء من غير أن يكون البعض أولى بالغرضية والتبعية من البعض. لا يقال معنى استناد الكل إليه ابتداء أنه الموجد بالاستقلال لكل ممكن لا أن ممكناً. وذلك الممكن ممكناً آخر على ما يراه الفلاسفة. وهذا لا ينافي توقف تحصيل البعض على البعض كالحركة على الجسم، والوصول إلى المنتهى على الحركة ونحو ذلك ما لا يحصى. لأنا نقول الذي يصلح أن يكون غرضاً لفعله ليس إلا إيصال اللذة إلى العبد، وهو مقدور له تعالى من غير شيء من الوسائط. وردّ بعد تسليم انحصار الغرض فيما ذكر بأن إيصال بعض اللذات قد لا يمكن إلا بخلق وسائط كالإحساس، ووجود ما يلتذ به ونحو ذلك. ومن الثاني وجهان: أحدهما أنه لا بد من انقطاع السلسلة إلى ما يكون (۲) غرضاً، ولا يكون لغرض، فلا يصح القول بلزوم الغرض وعمومه. وثانيهما أن مثل تخليد الكفار في النار لا يعقل فيه نفع لأحد، والحق أن تعليل بعض الأفعال لا سيما (۳) شرعية الأحكام (٤) بالحكم والمصالح ظاهر كإيجاب الحدود، والكفارات، وتحريم المسكرات وما أشبه ذلك، والنصوص أيضاً شاهدة بذلك كقوله تعالى وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون (٥) ومن أجل ذلك كتبنا على بني إسرائيل (١) الآية فلما قضى زيد منها وطراً زوجناكها لكيلا يكون على المؤمنين حرج (٧) الآية ولهذا كان القياس حجة إلا عند شرذمة لا يعتد بهم، وأما تعميم ذلك بأن لا يخلو فعل من أفعاله عن غرض فمحل بحث.
He said: That an act has a purpose is a necessity, and then the obligation returns. It was rejected by denying the necessity; rather, it is sufficient that it is merely for the benefit of others. And the second: If something among contingent things were a purpose for the act of the Creator, it would not be obtained by His creation originally, but by following that act and its mediation, because that is the meaning of purpose, and the necessary consequent is false because it is established that everything depends on Him originally, without some being more deserving of purpose and dependence than others. It cannot be said that the meaning of everything depending on Him originally is that He is the independent originator of every possible, not that a possible is the cause of another possible as the philosophers hold. This does not contradict the dependence of some things on others, like motion on body, and reaching the end on motion, and so on countless things. For we say: That which can be a purpose for His act is only the conveying of pleasure to the servant, and that is within His power without any means. And it was replied, after conceding that the purpose is limited to what was mentioned, that conveying some pleasures may not be possible except by creating means, like sensation and the existence of that which is enjoyed, etc. And from the second [argument] are two aspects: First, that the chain must terminate in that which is a purpose and has no purpose, so the statement of the necessity and generality of purpose is not valid. Second, that something like the eternal punishment of disbelievers is not conceivable as a benefit to anyone. The truth is that explaining some acts, especially legal rulings, by wisdom and benefits is apparent, like the imposition of [hadd] punishments, expiations, prohibition of intoxicants, and the like. And the texts also bear witness to that, like His saying, 'I created the jinn and mankind only to worship Me' (51:56), and 'Because of that We decreed upon the Children of Israel' (5:32) verse, and 'When Zayd had no longer need of her, We married her to you so that there would be no blame upon the believers' (33:37) verse. And therefore analogical reasoning is a proof except for a small group whose opinion is not considered. As for generalizing that, such that no act of His is devoid of purpose, that is a matter for discussion.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that all divine actions must have a purpose (gharad). The author begins by stating an objection: if a purpose is necessary for an act, then that brings back the initial problem (of making God's act dependent on something). This is countered by denying the necessity of purpose; it is enough that the act is simply for the benefit of others. The second part of the argument shows that if a contingent thing were a purpose for God's act, it would not be directly created but would follow through means, which is false because everything depends directly on God. A counterargument is considered: that the direct dependence does not exclude causal chains among creatures (e.g., motion depends on body). The author responds that what can be a purpose is only the conveyance of pleasure, which God can do without means. However, an objector replies that some pleasures require means like sensation. The author then presents two refutations of the necessity and universality of purpose: first, the chain of purposes must stop at something that is a purpose but not for another purpose, so universal purpose is unsustainable; second, eternal punishment of disbelievers has no benefit, so not all acts have a purpose. The author concedes that some acts, like legal rulings, have clear wisdoms, but this does not imply that every act does. Citing Quranic verses that show purposes for some acts, the author concludes that analogical reasoning (qiyas) is valid, but generalizing that every act has a purpose is debatable.

Key Terms
غرض
ضرورة
إلزام
ممكنات
وسائط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All divine actions must have a purpose that benefits someone.
Correction: While some acts have clear wisdoms, not all do; eternal punishment shows an act without benefit, and the chain of purposes must end somewhere.

Checkpoint
What is the author's first response to the objection that purpose is necessary?
A) He concedes but limits purposes to beneficial ones.
B) He denies the necessity and says it's enough that the act benefits others.
C) He argues that purpose is only for beneficial acts.
D) He says that purpose is necessary but not for all acts.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of purpose in every divine act is denied; it suffices that the act benefits others and God can directly grant pleasure without means.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an act of worship, do you secretly believe that God owes you something in return? How does knowing that God's acts require no benefit to Himself challenge that assumption? What can you do today to purify your intention so that it is purely for His sake?
?
The author argues that conveying pleasure to the servant is within God's power without any means. Do you live as if you believe that, or do you constantly seek intermediaries (like material means) and become anxious when they are absent? What would it look like to trust God's direct provision in one area of your life starting now?
?
If God's acts need not have a purpose from His side, what does that mean for your complaints about why certain trials happen? Are you willing to submit to His wisdom without demanding a reason, even when you cannot see the benefit? Make a concrete commitment to stop asking 'why' and start asking 'what now, Lord?'

Two Arguments Against Universal Purpose
Presents two arguments against universality of purpose and concedes limited purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two decisive arguments against the claim that every divine act has a purpose: the chain termination and the case of eternal punishment.

Core Idea
The chain of purposes must end, and eternal punishment has no benefit.

The previous lesson dealt with denying the necessity of purpose. Now the author presents two powerful arguments that show universal purpose is impossible: every chain of purposes must stop at a purposeless purpose, and the eternal punishment of disbelievers serves no benefit. The lesson also clarifies that some acts do have purposes, but not all.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Notice the two 'aspects' mentioned.
This passage continues from the previous.
2
Identify the first aspect: chain termination
The author argues that if everything has a purpose, we get an infinite regress or a circularity. The chain must end at something that is a purpose but has no purpose.
This is a standard infinite regress argument.
3
Identify the second aspect: eternal punishment
The punishment of disbelievers in Hell forever cannot be conceived as a benefit to anyone, so it lacks a purpose.
This is a concrete counterexample.
4
Understand the concession and conclusion
The author concedes that many acts (like legal rulings) have clear wisdoms supported by Quranic verses, but this does not mean every act has a purpose. Generalization is debatable.
The author uses qiyas as evidence for limited purpose.

?

Reward Does Not Indicate Desert; It Is Grace
Author argues that reward attached to works is not proof of desert, but a grace.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attachment of reward to works does not prove that works cause desert, but rather that it is a grace from Allah.

Core Idea
Reward accompanies works by divine grace, not by merit.

The objector argues that since Allah attaches reward to works, works must cause desert. But this inference is invalid. The reward could be a mere accompaniment of grace, not a recompense. This lesson unpacks the argument and its implications for understanding divine justice and grace.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the rhetorical questions in the middle.
2
Identify the objection and the core response
The objector claims that reward being tied to works means works are the cause. The author's core response is that it could be a grace (faḍl) accompanying the works, not a result of desert.
3
Understand the two supporting arguments
The author gives two rhetorical questions: (1) All actions are insufficient to thank for few bounties, so how can they deserve Paradise? (2) How can one deserve unimaginable reward for momentary faith? These reinforce that desert is not established.
These arguments highlight human incapacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثانياً: بأن ترتب الثواب على الأعمال لا يدل على أن لها تأثيراً في إثبات الاستحقاق لجواز أن يكون فضلاً من الله تعالى دائراً مع العمل، كيف وجميع الأفعال لا تفي لشكر القليل مما أفاض من النعماء، وكيف يعقل استحقاق ما لا عين رأت ولا أذن سمعت، ولا خطر على قلب بشر لمجرد تصديق القلب وإقرار اللسان فيمن آمن فمات في الحال. وبهذا يظهر أنه لا حاجة في إثبات الاستحقاق الى ما شرع من التكاليف على ما فصل في علم الفقه وعلم صفات القلب وأحوال الآخرة التي يسميه الإمام حجة الإسلام بعلم السر.
And second: that the attachment of reward to works does not indicate that they have an effect in establishing desert, because it is possible that it is a grace (faḍl) from Allah that accompanies the work. How so, while all actions are insufficient for the little thanks of the bounties He has bestowed. And how is it conceivable to deserve what no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to the human heart, merely for the assent of the heart and acknowledgment of the tongue in one who believed and died immediately? And by this it becomes clear that there is no need in establishing desert to what has been legislated of obligations, as detailed in the science of fiqh and the science of the states of the heart and the conditions of the hereafter, which Imam Ḥujjat al-Islām calls the science of the secret (ʿilm al-sirr).
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection and answer. The objector argued that the fact reward is attached to works indicates that works cause desert (istiḥqāq). The answer: this attachment does not prove causality; it could be that reward is a grace (faḍl) from God that accompanies the work by divine custom, not because the work merits it. The author gives two supporting arguments: (1) All human actions are insufficient to even thank God for the few bounties He has given, so how can they deserve eternal bliss? (2) How can one deserve Paradise, which is beyond imagination, merely by momentary faith and confession? This shows that establishing desert is not necessary; rather, it is God's grace. There is no need to prove desert through the legislated obligations (takālīf) as detailed in fiqh and the science of the heart (ʿilm al-sirr) of al-Ghazālī.

Key Terms
استحقاق
فضل
ثواب
شكر
علم السر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that reward being tied to works implies a causal relationship of desert.
Correction: The author shows that it may be a mere accompaniment by grace.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the attachment of reward to works does not prove desert?
A) Because works are too few to merit Paradise.
B) Because it could be a grace (فضل) that accompanies works.
C) Because reason cannot understand reward.
D) Because the Quran explicitly denies it.

Key Takeaway
The attachment of reward to works does not prove desert; it is a manifestation of divine grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that your good deeds earn you a place in Paradise? How does this passage challenge that belief, and what would it mean for you to truly accept that reward is pure grace?
?
If all your actions are insufficient to thank God for His blessings, how does that change the way you view your own obedience and worship? In what area of your life are you most prone to feeling that you deserve something from God?
?
The author says that even a momentary faith could be rewarded with unimaginable bliss as a grace. How does that make you feel about your own salvation? Are you relying on your deeds or on God's mercy?

Ash'ari and Mu'tazili on Divine Guidance and Misguidance
The author contrasts Ash'ari and Mu'tazili views on divine guidance and misguidance, with a methodological note and lexical clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological disagreement between the Ash'aris and Mu'tazila regarding divine guidance and misguidance, and why the Ash'ari position is considered more consistent with the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Divine guidance and misguidance are acts of creation, not mere metaphor.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid lays out the foundational dispute between the Ash'ari and Mu'tazili schools on whether God's guidance and misguidance mean He creates them in people or merely describes them. The author explains both positions and then criticizes the Mu'tazili view as relying on a flawed premise and contradicting many Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the arguments.
2
Identify the two contrasting views
Locate where the author presents the Ash'ari view (creation) and the Mu'tazili view (indication/punishment).
The phrase 'عندنا' signals the Ash'ari position, and 'وعند المعتزلة' introduces the Mu'tazili.
3
Analyze the Mu'tazili interpretation
Notice the multiple meanings they assign to guidance and misguidance, and why the author rejects them.
The rejection is based on their 'corrupt principle' and apparent Quranic meanings.
4
Understand the methodological context
Read the part about 'chapter of details of actions' to see where this discussion fits in the broader theological framework.
The author notes this is a standard follow-up to the creation of actions.
5
Review the lexical note on sealing
The footnote defines 'khatm' and 'tab'' as effects like sealing, and relates them to Quranic verses.
This clarifies the meaning of 'stamping hearts'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الخلاف في ما يدل على اتصاف الباري تعالى بالهداية والإضلال والطبع والختم (1) على قلوب الكفرة [المشركين في طغيانهم فعندنا بمعنى خلق الهدى والضلال لما ثبت من أنه الخالق وحده. وعند المعتزلة الهداية الدلالة الموصلة إلى البغية أو البيان بمعنى نصب الأدلة أو منح الألطاف، والإضلال الإهلاك والتعذيب أو التسمية والتلقيب بالضال، أو منع الألطاف أو الإسناد مجاز، وهذا مع ابتنائه على فاسد أصلهم يأباه ظاهر كثير من الآيات . قد جرت العادة بتعقيب مسألة خلق الأعمال بمباحث الهدى والضلال (۲) والأرزاق والآجال، ونحو ذلك، فعقدنا لها فصلاً وسميناه بفصل تفاريع الأفعال لا ابتناء عامة مباحثه على أنه تعالى هو الخالق لكل شيء ، وأنه لا قبح في خلقه وفعله، وإن قبح المخلوق. (۱) الختم والطبع : مصدرا ختمت وطبعت وهو تأثير الشي كنقش الخاتم والطابع ، والثاني: الأثر الحاصل عن الشيء ومنه قوله تعالى ختم الله على قلوبهم البقرة آية ٧ وقال بعضهم : ختمه شهادته تعالى عليه أنه لا يؤمن وقوله تعالى : اليوم نختم على أفواههم سورة يونس آية ٦٥ أي نمنعهم من الكلام .
As for the disagreement concerning what indicates that the Creator, exalted is He, is described with guidance and misguidance, and with sealing and stamping on the hearts of the disbelievers [the polytheists in their transgression]: with us, it means the creation of guidance and misguidance because it is established that He alone is the Creator. And with the Mu'tazila, guidance is the indication that leads to the desired object or the clarification in the sense of setting up proofs or granting favors, and misguidance is destruction and punishment, or naming and labeling as misguided, or withholding favors, or attribution metaphorically. And this, along with its being built upon their corrupt principle, is rejected by the apparent meaning of many verses. It is customary to follow up the issue of creation of actions with discussions of guidance and misguidance, and provisions and lifespans, and the like. So we have made a chapter for it and called it 'Chapter of Details of Actions' because the basis of all its discussions is that He, exalted, is the Creator of everything, and that there is no ugliness in His creation and His act, even if the created thing is ugly. (1) Al-khatm and al-tab': both are masdars of khatamt and taba't, and they are the effect of the thing like the engraving of the seal and the stamp; the second is the trace resulting from the thing, and from this is His statement, exalted: 'Allah has set a seal upon their hearts' (2:7). And some said: His sealing is His testimony that he will not believe. And His statement, exalted: 'Today We shall seal up their mouths' (36:65) meaning We prevent them from speaking.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazili position on divine guidance and misguidance, along with a methodological note and an explanatory lexical note. The author first presents the Ash'ari view: when God is described as guiding or misguiding, sealing or stamping hearts, this means He creates guidance or misguidance in the person, because He alone is the Creator. Then he presents the Mu'tazili view: guidance is merely indicating the right path or setting up proofs and granting favors, while misguidance is punishing, calling someone misguided, withholding favors, or metaphorical attribution. The author rejects this view because it is built on the Mu'tazili's corrupt principle (that God must do what is best for His servants) and contradicts many Quranic verses. Next, the author explains why he includes this discussion: it is customary to follow the topic of 'creation of actions' with discussions of guidance, misguidance, provisions, and lifespans. Hence he devotes a chapter called 'Chapter of Details of Actions' (Fasl Tafari' al-Af'al), whose basis is that God is the Creator of everything and that there is no ugliness in His actions, even if the created thing is ugly. Finally, a footnote defines 'al-khatm' (sealing) and 'al-tab'' (stamping) as effects like the impression of a seal or stamp, and cites Quranic verses about God sealing hearts and mouths, explaining that this means preventing them from believing or speaking.

خلق الأعمال
تفاريع الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila completely deny that God can be described as misguiding anyone.
Correction: The passage shows they allow attribution in the sense of punishment, naming, or withholding favors, not a complete denial.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari position in the passage, what does it mean when God is described as guiding or misguiding?
A) It means He indicates the right path and sets up proofs.
B) It means He creates guidance or misguidance in the person.
C) It means He names the person guided or misguided.
D) It is purely metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'aris affirm that God creates guidance and misguidance directly, while the Mu'tazila reinterpret them as indicating and punishing—a view the author rejects as inconsistent with the Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your guidance is solely from God, or do you subtly attribute it to your own efforts? How does that affect your humility and gratitude?
?
When you read about God sealing hearts, do you fear that your own heart might be sealed due to persistent sin? What will you do today to soften it and seek His guidance?
?
If God's creation of misguidance is not unjust, why do you still question His decrees when things go wrong? Can you accept His absolute sovereignty over your life without resentment?

The Quranic Verses on Divine Guidance and Misguidance
Citing Quranic verses and stating the Ash'ari position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key Quranic verses that describe God's guidance and misguidance, and the Ash'ari claim that these refer to God's actual creation of faith and disbelief.

Core Idea
God's guidance and misguidance are real acts of creation, not mere metaphors.

This lesson introduces the Quranic foundation for the Ash'ari doctrine of divine guidance and misguidance. The passage cites several verses where God attributes guidance, misguidance, sealing of hearts, and other actions directly to Himself. According to the Ash'ari school, these verses must be taken literally: God creates both faith and disbelief, as He is the sole creator. This sets the stage for the debate with the Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the first part of the source passage, which lists the Quranic verses. Focus on the variety of expressions used: دعا, هدى, شرح الصدر, طبع على القلوب, etc.
These verses are the starting point for the theological argument.
2
Identify the Ash'ari position
Notice that after quoting the verses, the author states the Ash'ari view: these verses refer to God's creation of faith and disbelief. This is based on the principle that God alone is the creator.
The Ash'ari position is a literal reading of the verses.
3
Contrast with the Mu'tazila view
The author then introduces the Mu'tazila objection: if God created both, reward and punishment would be meaningless. This contrast helps understand the core dispute.
The Mu'tazila insist on human free will to justify moral responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام في الآيات المشتملة على اتصاف الباري تعالى بالهداية والإضلال والطبع على قلوب الكفرة والختم والمد في طغيانهم ونحو ذلك كقوله تعالى والله يدعو إلى دار السلام ويهدي من يشاء إلى صراط مستقيم وإنك لا تهدي من أحببت ولكن الله يهدي من يشاء فمن يرد الله أن يهديه يشرح صدره للإسلام، ومن يرد أن يضله يجعله صدره ضيقاً حرجاً من يهد الله فهو المهتدي ومن يضلل فأولئك هم الخاسرون إن هي إلا فتنتك تضل بها من تشاء وتهدي من تشاء ويضل به كثيراً ويهدي به كثيراً وختم الله على قلوبهم بل طبع الله عليها بكفرهم وجعلنا على قلوبهم أكنة أن يفقهوه ويمدهم في طغيانهم إلى غير ذلك. فهي عندنا راجعة إلى خلق الإيمان والاهتداء، والكفر والضلال بناء على ما مر من أنه الخالق وحده خلافاً للمعتزلة بناء على أصلهم الفاسد. أنه لو خلق فيهم الإيمان والضلال لما صح منه المدح والثواب والذم والعقاب فحملوا الهداية على الإرشاد إلى طريق الحق بالبيان، ونصب الأدلة أو الإرشاد في الآخرة إلى طريق الجنة، والإضلال على الإهلاك والتعذيب أو التسمية والتثبيت والتلقيب بالضال أو الوجدان ضالاً ولما ظهر على بعضهم أن بعض هذه المعاني تقبل التعليق بالمشيئة وبعضها لا يخص المؤمن دون الكافر، وبعضها ليس مضافاً إلى الله تعالى دون النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وبعض معاني الإضلال لا يقابل الهداية، جعلوا الهداية بمعنى الدلالة الموصلة إلى النعيم والإضلال مع أنه فعل الشيطان مسنداً إلى الله تعالى مجازاً لما أنه بأقداره، وتمكينه، ولأن ضلالهم بواسطة ضربه المثل في يضل به كثيراً أو بواسطة الفتنة التي هي الابتلاء والتكليف في تضل بها من تشاء ونحن نقول: بل الهداية هي الدلالة على الطريق الموصل سواء كانت موصلة أم لا والعدول إلى المجاز، إنما ليصح عند تعذر الحقيقة ولا تعذر وبعض المواضع من كلام الله تعالى يشهد للمتأمل بأن إضافة الهداية والإضلال إلى الله تعالى ليست إلا بطريق الحقيقة والله الهادي.
As for the discussion concerning the verses that include the description of the Exalted Creator with guidance (al-hidaya) and misguidance (al-idlal), sealing the hearts of the disbelievers, closing them, and extending them in their transgression, and similar matters, such as His saying: 'And Allah invites to the abode of peace and guides whom He wills to a straight path' and 'Indeed you cannot guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills' and 'So whoever Allah wills to guide, He expands his breast for Islam, and whoever He wills to misguide, He makes his breast narrow, constricted' and 'Whom Allah guides, he is the guided one, and whom He misguides, those are the losers' and 'It is only Your trial; You mislead by it whom You will and guide whom You will' and 'He misleads many thereby and guides many thereby' and 'Allah has set a seal upon their hearts' and 'Rather, Allah has set a seal upon them for their disbelief' and 'And We have placed over their hearts coverings lest they understand it' and 'And We extend them in their transgression' and so forth. These, in our view, refer to the creation of faith and guidance, and disbelief and misguidance, based on what has passed that He alone is the Creator, contrary to the Mu'tazila based on their corrupt principle: that if He created faith and misguidance in them, then praise, reward, blame, and punishment would not be valid from Him. So they interpreted al-hidaya as guidance to the path of truth through clarification and setting up proofs, or guidance in the Hereafter to the path of Paradise; and al-idlal as destruction and punishment, or naming and confirming and labeling as misguided, or finding him misguided. And when it became apparent to some of them that some of these meanings can be attached to will, and some are not specific to the believer as opposed to the disbeliever, and some are not attributed to Allah without the Prophet (peace be upon him), and some meanings of idlal do not correspond to hidaya, they made hidaya meaning 'the guidance that leads to bliss' and idlal, although it is the act of Satan, is attributed metaphorically to Allah because it is by His decrees and enabling, and because their misguidance is through His striking of the parable in 'He misleads many thereby' or through the trial that is the test and obligation in 'You mislead by it whom You will.' And we say: Rather, al-hidaya is indication of the way that reaches, whether it actually reaches or not. And resorting to metaphor is only valid when the literal meaning is impossible, and it is not impossible. And some places in the speech of Allah testify to the contemplator that the attribution of hidaya and idlal to Allah is only in a literal sense. And Allah is the Guide.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the Ash'ari position on divine guidance and misguidance. It begins by citing numerous Quranic verses where God attributes guidance, misguidance, sealing of hearts, etc., to Himself. The author then states the Ash'ari view: these verses refer to God's actual creation of faith and disbelief, as He is the sole creator. He then presents the Mu'tazila objection based on their principle that if God created both, reward and punishment would be meaningless. The Mu'tazila therefore reinterpret the verses: hidaya is merely guidance through proofs, and idlal is destruction or mere labeling. The author then notes inconsistencies in the Mu'tazila position: some reinterpretations cannot apply to will, are not exclusive to believers, or are not solely attributed to God. The Mu'tazila then shifted to defining hidaya as 'guidance that actually reaches bliss' and idlal as metaphorically from God because He permits it. The author's rebuttal asserts that hidaya is simply 'indication of the way' regardless of result, and metaphor is unnecessary since literalism is possible. He concludes that the Quranic evidence supports the literal attribution of guidance and misguidance to God.

هداية
إضلال
خلق الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari position presented in this passage, what do the Quranic verses about guidance and misguidance refer to?
A) Mere metaphorical descriptions
B) God's creation of faith and disbelief
C) Only guidance, not misguidance
D) Human free will choices

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school interprets Quranic verses on guidance and misguidance literally as God's creation of faith and disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'Allah guides whom He wills and leads astray whom He wills', do you truly believe that your own faith is entirely a gift from Him? How does that realization humble you right now, and what specific prayer for steadfastness will you make today?
?
The lesson shows that even misguidance is a creation of God, yet it is a just consequence of disbelief. Have you ever blamed circumstances or other people for your own spiritual failures, forgetting that your choices lead to God's response? What will you change today to take responsibility while relying solely on Him?
?
Read the verse from the passage: 'إن هي إلا فتنتك تضل بها من تشاء وتهدي من تشاء'. This test (fitna) includes both guidance and misguidance. In your life, how do you see God testing you through the people around you who have turned away? Will you now pray for them differently, acknowledging that only He can grant guidance?

Mu'tazila Reinterpretation of Divine Guidance
Presenting Mu'tazila objection and initial reinterpretations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila argument against God creating misguidance and their initial reinterpretation of the relevant Quranic terms.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila deny God creates misguidance to preserve divine justice and human responsibility.

The Mu'tazila objected to the literal reading of the verses because they believed it would undermine divine justice: if God creates both faith and disbelief, then reward and punishment become meaningless. To resolve this, they reinterpreted key terms. This lesson explores their initial reinterpretations and the problems that arose from them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila principle
Read the part where the author states the Mu'tazila principle: if God created faith and misguidance, praise, reward, blame, and punishment would not be valid. This is based on their view of human free will.
This principle is central to Mu'tazila theology.
2
Learn their reinterpretations
The Mu'tazila reinterpreted 'hidaya' as guidance through proofs (irshad) and 'idlal' as destruction or labeling. note how they try to avoid attributing creation of misguidance to God.
They use metaphorical interpretations to reconcile verses with their principle.
3
Identify the inconsistencies
The author points out that some of these reinterpretations failed certain criteria: some meanings cannot apply to will, some are not exclusive to believers, etc. This leads to further adjustments.
The Mu'tazila were forced to modify their interpretations.

?

?

Ash'ari Rebuttal: Literal Meaning is Possible
Ash'ari rebuttal: literal meaning is possible and supported by the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari rebuttal against the Mu'tazila, asserting that a literal interpretation of the verses is both possible and supported by the Quran.

Core Idea
Metaphor is only used when literal meaning is impossible; here it is not.

After presenting the Mu'tazila reinterpretations, the author delivers the Ash'ari counterargument. He argues that the Mu'tazila resorted to metaphor unnecessarily, because the literal meaning of the verses is not impossible. Moreover, he points to Quranic evidence that supports the literal attribution of guidance and misguidance to God. This lesson concludes the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari definition of hidaya
The author defines hidaya as 'indication of the way that reaches' (al-dalala 'ala al-tariq al-muwassil), regardless of whether it actually reaches. This is a key distinction.
This definition allows God to guide without necessarily bringing about faith.
2
Understand the principle of metaphor
The author states that resorting to metaphor is only valid when the literal meaning is impossible. Since the literal meaning is not impossible, the Mu'tazila's move is unwarranted.
This is a methodological point in theological interpretation.
3
See the Quranic evidence for literalism
The author asserts that many places in the Quran testify that the attribution of guidance and misguidance to God is literal. This reinforces the Ash'ari position.
The argument is not just philosophical but grounded in scripture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام في الآيات المشتملة على اتصاف الباري تعالى بالهداية والإضلال والطبع على قلوب الكفرة والختم والمد في طغيانهم ونحو ذلك كقوله تعالى والله يدعو إلى دار السلام ويهدي من يشاء إلى صراط مستقيم وإنك لا تهدي من أحببت ولكن الله يهدي من يشاء فمن يرد الله أن يهديه يشرح صدره للإسلام، ومن يرد أن يضله يجعله صدره ضيقاً حرجاً من يهد الله فهو المهتدي ومن يضلل فأولئك هم الخاسرون إن هي إلا فتنتك تضل بها من تشاء وتهدي من تشاء ويضل به كثيراً ويهدي به كثيراً وختم الله على قلوبهم بل طبع الله عليها بكفرهم وجعلنا على قلوبهم أكنة أن يفقهوه ويمدهم في طغيانهم إلى غير ذلك. فهي عندنا راجعة إلى خلق الإيمان والاهتداء، والكفر والضلال بناء على ما مر من أنه الخالق وحده خلافاً للمعتزلة بناء على أصلهم الفاسد. أنه لو خلق فيهم الإيمان والضلال لما صح منه المدح والثواب والذم والعقاب فحملوا الهداية على الإرشاد إلى طريق الحق بالبيان، ونصب الأدلة أو الإرشاد في الآخرة إلى طريق الجنة، والإضلال على الإهلاك والتعذيب أو التسمية والتثبيت والتلقيب بالضال أو الوجدان ضالاً ولما ظهر على بعضهم أن بعض هذه المعاني تقبل التعليق بالمشيئة وبعضها لا يخص المؤمن دون الكافر، وبعضها ليس مضافاً إلى الله تعالى دون النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وبعض معاني الإضلال لا يقابل الهداية، جعلوا الهداية بمعنى الدلالة الموصلة إلى النعيم والإضلال مع أنه فعل الشيطان مسنداً إلى الله تعالى مجازاً لما أنه بأقداره، وتمكينه، ولأن ضلالهم بواسطة ضربه المثل في يضل به كثيراً أو بواسطة الفتنة التي هي الابتلاء والتكليف في تضل بها من تشاء ونحن نقول: بل الهداية هي الدلالة على الطريق الموصل سواء كانت موصلة أم لا والعدول إلى المجاز، إنما ليصح عند تعذر الحقيقة ولا تعذر وبعض المواضع من كلام الله تعالى يشهد للمتأمل بأن إضافة الهداية والإضلال إلى الله تعالى ليست إلا بطريق الحقيقة والله الهادي.
As for the discussion concerning the verses that include the description of the Exalted Creator with guidance (al-hidaya) and misguidance (al-idlal), sealing the hearts of the disbelievers, closing them, and extending them in their transgression, and similar matters, such as His saying: 'And Allah invites to the abode of peace and guides whom He wills to a straight path' and 'Indeed you cannot guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills' and 'So whoever Allah wills to guide, He expands his breast for Islam, and whoever He wills to misguide, He makes his breast narrow, constricted' and 'Whom Allah guides, he is the guided one, and whom He misguides, those are the losers' and 'It is only Your trial; You mislead by it whom You will and guide whom You will' and 'He misleads many thereby and guides many thereby' and 'Allah has set a seal upon their hearts' and 'Rather, Allah has set a seal upon them for their disbelief' and 'And We have placed over their hearts coverings lest they understand it' and 'And We extend them in their transgression' and so forth. These, in our view, refer to the creation of faith and guidance, and disbelief and misguidance, based on what has passed that He alone is the Creator, contrary to the Mu'tazila based on their corrupt principle: that if He created faith and misguidance in them, then praise, reward, blame, and punishment would not be valid from Him. So they interpreted al-hidaya as guidance to the path of truth through clarification and setting up proofs, or guidance in the Hereafter to the path of Paradise; and al-idlal as destruction and punishment, or naming and confirming and labeling as misguided, or finding him misguided. And when it became apparent to some of them that some of these meanings can be attached to will, and some are not specific to the believer as opposed to the disbeliever, and some are not attributed to Allah without the Prophet (peace be upon him), and some meanings of idlal do not correspond to hidaya, they made hidaya meaning 'the guidance that leads to bliss' and idlal, although it is the act of Satan, is attributed metaphorically to Allah because it is by His decrees and enabling, and because their misguidance is through His striking of the parable in 'He misleads many thereby' or through the trial that is the test and obligation in 'You mislead by it whom You will.' And we say: Rather, al-hidaya is indication of the way that reaches, whether it actually reaches or not. And resorting to metaphor is only valid when the literal meaning is impossible, and it is not impossible. And some places in the speech of Allah testify to the contemplator that the attribution of hidaya and idlal to Allah is only in a literal sense. And Allah is the Guide.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the Ash'ari position on divine guidance and misguidance. It begins by citing numerous Quranic verses where God attributes guidance, misguidance, sealing of hearts, etc., to Himself. The author then states the Ash'ari view: these verses refer to God's actual creation of faith and disbelief, as He is the sole creator. He then presents the Mu'tazila objection based on their principle that if God created both, reward and punishment would be meaningless. The Mu'tazila therefore reinterpret the verses: hidaya is merely guidance through proofs, and idlal is destruction or mere labeling. The author then notes inconsistencies in the Mu'tazila position: some reinterpretations cannot apply to will, are not exclusive to believers, or are not solely attributed to God. The Mu'tazila then shifted to defining hidaya as 'guidance that actually reaches bliss' and idlal as metaphorically from God because He permits it. The author's rebuttal asserts that hidaya is simply 'indication of the way' regardless of result, and metaphor is unnecessary since literalism is possible. He concludes that the Quranic evidence supports the literal attribution of guidance and misguidance to God.

Key Terms
هداية
حقيقة
مجاز
دلالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari rebuttal, when is resorting to metaphor valid?
A) When the literal meaning is impossible
B) When the literal meaning is unclear
C) When it supports divine justice
D) When it is used in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school argues that a literal interpretation of divine guidance and misguidance is both possible and Scripturally supported.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the definition of hidaya: 'indication of the way that reaches whether or not it actually reaches'. Do you truly believe that Allah has shown you the way even when you have not followed it? How does that affect your accountability today? Will you thank Him for the indication and take one concrete step to follow it this week?
?
If you have ever doubted Allah's guidance because of your own sins, how does this lesson's definition remove that doubt? Are you willing to trust that His indication is sufficient and respond with action?
?
The author says metaphor is only used when literal meaning is impossible. Are there areas of your belief where you have metaphorically explained away Allah's attributes to avoid personal responsibility? What would change if you took His attributes literally, especially al-Hadi?

Guidance and Misguidance: The Foundational Verses and Ash'ari Position
The author cites Quranic verses and states the Ash'ari position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that guidance and misguidance are literal acts of God creating faith and disbelief, supported by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
God alone creates both faith and disbelief; guidance and misguidance are His literal acts.

The author begins by citing several Quranic verses that explicitly attribute guidance and misguidance to Allah. These verses form the scriptural foundation for the Ash'ari position. As you read, notice how each verse uses active verbs for God's role in guiding or misguiding.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses cited
Read the Arabic verses and their translation. Notice the pattern: God directly guides or misguides individuals.
Verses include 'You misguide whom You will and guide whom You will' and 'He misguides many thereby and guides many thereby.'
2
Identify the Ash'ari conclusion
After listing verses, the author states the Ash'ari position: these refer to God's creation of faith and guidance, and disbelief and misguidance.
This is based on the principle that God alone is the Creator of all actions.
3
Understand the basis
The Ash'ari position is built on the earlier discussed principle that God is the sole Creator. Reflect on why this leads to the literal interpretation.

Al-huda (guidance): 'It is nothing but a trial from You by which You misguide whom You will and guide whom You will' (1) and 'He misguides many thereby and guides many thereby' (2) and 'And God has sealed their hearts' (3) and 'Rather, God has set a seal upon them for their disbelief' (4) and 'And We have placed upon their hearts covers lest they understand it' (5) and 'And We increase them in their transgression' (6) and so forth. So these [verses] in our view refer to the creation of faith and guidance, and disbelief and misguidance, based on what has passed that He alone is the Creator, contrary to the Mu'tazila based on their corrupt principle that if He created faith and guidance in them and disbelief and misguidance, then praise, reward, blame, and punishment would not be valid from Him. So they interpreted guidance (al-hidaya) as indication (al-irshad) to the path of truth by explanation and the erection of proofs, or indication in the Hereafter to the path of Paradise; and misguidance (al-idlal) as destruction and torment, or naming and confirming (al-tathbit) (8) and labeling as misguided, or finding [one] misguided. And when it became apparent to some of them that some of these meanings admit of being attached to [God's] will, and some of them are not specific to the believer as opposed to the disbeliever, and some of them are not attributed to God Almighty as opposed to the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, and some of the meanings of misguidance do not correspond to guidance, they made guidance to mean the indication that leads to bliss (al-na'im) and misguidance, even though it is the act of Satan, as being metaphorically attributed to God Almighty because it occurs by His decrees and enabling, and because their misguidance is through His striking of the example in 'He misguides many thereby' (10) or through the trial which is the test and obligation in 'You misguide thereby whom You will' (11). And we say: Rather, guidance is the indication of the way that leads, whether it actually leads or not, and turning to metaphor is only valid when the literal meaning is impossible, and it is not impossible. And some places in the speech of God Almighty testify to the one who reflects that the attribution of guidance and misguidance to God Almighty is only in a literal sense. And God is the Guide.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument regarding the interpretation of Quranic verses about guidance (huda) and misguidance (idlal). The author defends the Ash'ari position that God is the sole creator of both guidance and misguidance, and that these are literal acts of God, contrary to the Mu'tazila who reinterpret them to avoid attributing evil to God. The author begins by citing several Quranic verses that predicate guidance and misguidance to God. He then states the Ash'ari position: these verses refer to God's creation of faith and guidance, and disbelief and misguidance, based on the principle that God alone is the Creator. He then presents the Mu'tazila objection: if God created disbelief and misguidance in people, then divine praise, reward, blame, and punishment would not be valid. To avoid this, the Mu'tazila reinterpret hidaya as mere indication (irshad) and idlal as destruction or naming, etc. The author then notes that some Mu'tazila realized inconsistencies in these reinterpretations (e.g., some meanings are not exclusive to believers, some are not attributed to God, etc.), so they further refined their interpretation: hidaya is the indication that leads to bliss, and idlal is attributed to God metaphorically as it occurs by His decrees and through Satan's action or through trials. The author then presents the Ash'ari response: hidaya is simply indication of the way that leads, regardless of whether it actually leads; resorting to metaphor is only justified when the literal meaning is impossible, but here it is not impossible. Moreover, many Quranic verses show that the attribution is literal. The passage concludes with 'And God is the Guide.'

الإضلال
خلق الأفعال

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Quranic verses about guidance and misguidance are merely metaphorical or do not indicate God's direct creation of these states.
Correction: The passage shows that these verses are taken literally by the Ash'aris to mean God creates faith and disbelief.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'aris interpret Quranic verses about guidance and misguidance literally as God's creation of faith and disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that God 'seals hearts' and 'leads astray whom He wills', do you recognize that your own faith is entirely dependent on His mercy, not your merit? If He withdrew His guidance, could you remain a believer? Take a moment to plead for His steadfastness.
?
If you truly believe that God alone creates both guidance and misguidance, does that humble you? Or does it secretly anger you? Examine your heart: are you grateful that He guided you while others are left in misguidance, or do you feel a sense of superiority? Today, commit to thanking Him for a gift you did not earn.

The Mu'tazila Interpretation of Guidance and Misguidance
The author presents Mu'tazila reinterpretations and their refinements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila reinterpretations of guidance and misguidance and their motivations.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila reinterpret hidaya as mere indication and idlal as punishment to avoid attributing evil to God.

After presenting the Ash'ari view, the author now explains the Mu'tazila position. They reject that God creates disbelief, so they reinterpret guidance and misguidance in ways that avoid direct divine causation of evil. This lesson explores their various interpretations and the inconsistencies that arose.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila objection
Start with their principle: if God created disbelief, then praise and blame would not be valid. Understand their reasoning.
2
Identify the reinterpretations of hidaya
They say hidaya is 'indication to the path of truth by explanation and proofs.' Note this removes actual causation.
3
Identify the reinterpretations of idlal
They say idlal is destruction, torment, naming as misguided, or finding someone misguided. These are not direct creation of misguidance.
4
See the refinements
The author notes that some Mu'tazila realized problems with these meanings, so they further refined: hidaya is indication that leads to bliss, and idlal is attributed metaphorically to God via Satan or trials.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse that seems to attribute something negative to Allah, does your heart immediately seek to reinterpret it like the Mu'tazila did? What does that say about your trust in Allah's perfect wisdom and justice? Will you let the Quran speak for itself, or will you impose your own logic onto it?
?
The Mu'tazila were so concerned with protecting Allah's justice that they reinterpreted clear texts. Have you ever twisted a truth in your own life to protect your own comfort or reputation? Are you willing to accept uncomfortable truths about yourself that Allah reveals through His speech?
?
The Mu'tazila's reinterpretation led to internal inconsistencies and refinements. Are there areas of your faith where you have compromised or rationalized to avoid a difficult truth? Ask Allah tonight to show you where you have been like the Mu'tazila—more concerned with your own reasoning than with submitting to His revelation.

The Ash'ari Refutation: Literal Meaning of Hidaya and Idlal
The author presents the Ash'ari response: literal interpretation of hidaya and idlal is valid and supported by Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that guidance and misguidance must be taken literally and the refutation of the Mu'tazila metaphorical interpretation.

Core Idea
Hidaya is simply indication of the way that leads, and literal interpretation is valid since no impossibility prevents it.

Having presented the Mu'tazila reinterpretations, the author now delivers the Ash'ari response. The core argument is that guidance is straightforward: it means showing the way that leads to the goal, regardless of whether the person actually reaches it. Metaphor is only used when the literal meaning is impossible, and here it is not. The author also points to Quranic evidence for the literal attribution.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Ash'ari definition of hidaya
They define hidaya as 'indication of the way that leads' (al-dalala 'ala al-tariq al-muwassil). Note that it does not require the person to actually reach the destination.
2
See the argument against metaphor
The author argues that resorting to metaphor is only justified when the literal meaning is impossible. Since it is not impossible for God to create guidance and misguidance, the literal meaning must be retained.
3
Consider the Quranic evidence
The author claims that many Quranic verses testify to the literal attribution of guidance and misguidance to God. Reflect on the verses cited earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الهدى إن هي إلا فتنتك تضل بها من تشاء وتهدي من (1) ويضل به كثيراً ويهدي به كثيراً) (۲) وختم الله على قلوبهم ) (۳) بل طبع الله عليها بكفرهم) وجعلنا على قلوبهم أكنة أن يفقهوه ) (٥) و ويمدهم في طغيانهم (٦) إلى غير ذلك. فهي عندنا راجعة إلى خلق الإيمان والاهتداء، والكفر والضلال بناء على ما مر من أنه الخالق وحده خلافاً للمعتزلة بناء على أصلهم الفاسد. أنه لو خلق فيهم ) والضلال لما صح منه المدح والثواب والذم والعقاب فحملوا الهداية على الإرشاد إلى طريق الحق بالبيان، ونصب الأدلة أو الإرشاد في الآخرة إلى طريق الجنة ، والإضلال على الإهلاك والتعذيب أو التسمية والتثبيت (۸) والتلقيب بالضال أو الوجدان ضالاً ولما ظهر على بعضهم أن بعض هذه المعاني تقبل التعليق بالمشيئة وبعضها لا يخص المؤمن دون الكافر، وبعضها ليس مضافاً إلى الله تعالى دون النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وبعض معاني الإضلال لا يقابل الهداية ، جعلوا الهداية بمعنى الدلالة الموصلة إلى النعيم والإضلال مع أنه فعل الشيطان مسنداً إلى الله تعالى مجازاً لما أنه بأقداره، وتمكينه، ولأن ضلالهم بواسطة ضربه المثل في يضل به كثيراً (١٠) أو بواسطة الفتنة التي هي الابتلاء والتكليف في تضل بها من تشاء (۱۱) ونحن نقول : بل الهداية هي الدلالة على الطريق الموصل سواء كانت موصلة أم لا والعدول إلى المجاز، إنما ليصح عند تعذر الحقيقة ولا تعذر وبعض المواضع من كلام الله تعالى يشهد للمتأمل بأن إضافة الهداية والإضلال إلى الله تعالى ليست إلا بطريق الحقيقة والله الهادي.
Al-huda (guidance): 'It is nothing but a trial from You by which You misguide whom You will and guide whom You will' (1) and 'He misguides many thereby and guides many thereby' (2) and 'And God has sealed their hearts' (3) and 'Rather, God has set a seal upon them for their disbelief' (4) and 'And We have placed upon their hearts covers lest they understand it' (5) and 'And We increase them in their transgression' (6) and so forth. So these [verses] in our view refer to the creation of faith and guidance, and disbelief and misguidance, based on what has passed that He alone is the Creator, contrary to the Mu'tazila based on their corrupt principle that if He created faith and guidance in them and disbelief and misguidance, then praise, reward, blame, and punishment would not be valid from Him. So they interpreted guidance (al-hidaya) as indication (al-irshad) to the path of truth by explanation and the erection of proofs, or indication in the Hereafter to the path of Paradise; and misguidance (al-idlal) as destruction and torment, or naming and confirming (al-tathbit) (8) and labeling as misguided, or finding [one] misguided. And when it became apparent to some of them that some of these meanings admit of being attached to [God's] will, and some of them are not specific to the believer as opposed to the disbeliever, and some of them are not attributed to God Almighty as opposed to the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, and some of the meanings of misguidance do not correspond to guidance, they made guidance to mean the indication that leads to bliss (al-na'im) and misguidance, even though it is the act of Satan, as being metaphorically attributed to God Almighty because it occurs by His decrees and enabling, and because their misguidance is through His striking of the example in 'He misguides many thereby' (10) or through the trial which is the test and obligation in 'You misguide thereby whom You will' (11). And we say: Rather, guidance is the indication of the way that leads, whether it actually leads or not, and turning to metaphor is only valid when the literal meaning is impossible, and it is not impossible. And some places in the speech of God Almighty testify to the one who reflects that the attribution of guidance and misguidance to God Almighty is only in a literal sense. And God is the Guide.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument regarding the interpretation of Quranic verses about guidance (huda) and misguidance (idlal). The author defends the Ash'ari position that God is the sole creator of both guidance and misguidance, and that these are literal acts of God, contrary to the Mu'tazila who reinterpret them to avoid attributing evil to God. The author begins by citing several Quranic verses that predicate guidance and misguidance to God. He then states the Ash'ari position: these verses refer to God's creation of faith and guidance, and disbelief and misguidance, based on the principle that God alone is the Creator. He then presents the Mu'tazila objection: if God created disbelief and misguidance in people, then divine praise, reward, blame, and punishment would not be valid. To avoid this, the Mu'tazila reinterpret hidaya as mere indication (irshad) and idlal as destruction or naming, etc. The author then notes that some Mu'tazila realized inconsistencies in these reinterpretations (e.g., some meanings are not exclusive to believers, some are not attributed to God, etc.), so they further refined their interpretation: hidaya is the indication that leads to bliss, and idlal is attributed to God metaphorically as it occurs by His decrees and through Satan's action or through trials. The author then presents the Ash'ari response: hidaya is simply indication of the way that leads, regardless of whether it actually leads; resorting to metaphor is only justified when the literal meaning is impossible, but here it is not impossible. Moreover, many Quranic verses show that the attribution is literal. The passage concludes with 'And God is the Guide.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That hidaya must always result in the person being guided (i.e., faith).
Correction: The Ash'aris define hidaya as indication of the way that leads, regardless of outcome.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari response, when is it valid to use metaphorical interpretation of a Quranic term?
A) When the literal meaning is unclear
B) When the literal meaning is impossible
C) When it supports a particular theological position
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Hidaya is literal indication of the way that leads; metaphor is unwarranted because literal meaning is possible and supported by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's guidance, do you truly believe that He has given you sufficient indication of the right path, even if you sometimes fail to reach it? How does this passage challenge any hidden resentment you harbor toward Allah for your own missteps?
?
If hidaya is merely the indication of the way and not forced arrival, how does that reshape your daily reliance on Allah? Are you content to simply receive His signs, or do you secretly demand that He drag you to paradise against your will?
?
In which area of your life have you been using the 'impossible' excuse to avoid taking responsibility, while this lesson teaches you that literal commands are possible and binding? Write down one specific command you have been treating as metaphorical that you will now obey literally.
